So the `video_set_backlight_video_vendor` callback:1. Disables the ACER_CAP_BRIGHTNESS capability \n2. Prints a message \"Brightness must be controlled by generic video driver\"\n\nThis function is used for models in the video_vendor_dmi_table that are marked with .callback = video_set_backlight_video_vendor.\n\nFor models WITHOUT a callback (like the KAV80), they are NOT supposed to use this function. Instead, they are identified as models where \"we must use the acer interface, as there is no native backlight interface.\"\n\nNow, looking at the logic:1. Models WITH callback video_set_backlight_video_vendor: disable ACER brightness, use generic video driver\n2. Models WITHOUT callback (like KAV80): use the acer WMI interface\n\nThe issue is:- TravelMate 5735Z is NOT in the video_vendor_dmi_table at all\n- So the acer_wmi driver doesn't know about it\n- At line 2210-2211, since acpi_video_get_backlight_type() probably returns acpi_backlight_video (not acpi_backlight_vendor), it disables the acer brightness capability\n\nBut what should happen?- With acpi_backlight=native, it works\n- This suggests that the native backlight interface works on this device\n\nLooking at the bug report again:- By default: intel_backlight is available but doesn't work when triggered by function keys, shows 5 levels from acer_wmi (but acer brightness is disabled?)\n- With acpi_backlight=native: native backlight interface works, 15-16 levels\n\nActually, I think I misunderstood. Let me re-read the bug report:\n\n\"There is only `/sys/class/backlight/intel_backlight/brightness` though, and writing values to it seems to work.\"\n\nSo writing to intel_backlight directly works, but:1. GNOME OSD shows 5 levels from acer_wmi\n\n\n2. The hardware function keys don't trigger any brightness adjustment\n\nThe root cause appears to be that acer_wmi brightness is disabled, so the function keys—which are supposed to trigger acer_wmi brightness changes—don't respond. When acpi_backlight=native is set, the native ACPI video interface takes control instead, enabling both the function keys and providing the full 15-16 brightness levels.\n\nThe device likely needs either the native ACPI video backlight or acer_wmi backlight to work properly, but the generic acpi_video driver isn't initializing brightness correctly for this model.
